      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21164-1" target="تَسَوَّدُوا" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">تَتَسَوَّدُوا</foreign>], (O,) meaning <hi rend="ital">Learn ye knowledge,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">science, before ye be</hi> [<hi rend="ital">made</hi>] <hi rend="ital">chiefs,</hi> looked at; for if ye learn not before that, ye will be ashamed to learn after becoming advanced in age, or attaining to full growth, (<foreign lang="ar">بَعْدَ الكِبَرِ</foreign>,) and so will remain ignorant, taking it [i. e. knowledge] from the younger ones, and that will lower your estima- <pb n="1461"/> tion: (M:) or the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">before ye be married, and become masters of houses,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tents,</hi> and be diverted by the marriage-state from [the acquisition of] knowledge, or science.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21189-1" target="أَسْوَدِىٌّ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21192"/></foreign> signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign>: (Ham p. 379:) [or has an intensive signification, like <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَرىٌّ</foreign>:] the fem. of <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">سَوْدَآءُ</foreign>: (Mgh, Msb:) the dim. of <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign> is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21189-2" target="أُسَيِّدُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21194"/></foreign>, (S, Msb,) and it is allowable to say   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21189-3" target="أُسَيْوِدُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, [as is shown by an ex. voce <foreign lang="ar">أَسَكُّ</foreign>,] meaning [<hi rend="ital">a little black thing;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">blackish,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">approaching to black;</hi> (S;) and the abbreviated dim. is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21189-4" target="سُوَيْدٌ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21183"/></foreign>: (S, Mgh, Msb:) the dim. of <foreign lang="ar">سَوْدَآءُ</foreign> is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21189-5" target="سُوَيْدَآءُ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21187"/></foreign>: (Mgh:) the pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign> (M, Msb) and of <foreign lang="ar">سَوْدَآءُ</foreign> (Msb) is <foreign lang="ar">سُودٌ</foreign> (M, Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">سُودَانٌ</foreign> [which latter is especially applied to human beings]. (M.) <foreign lang="ar">السُّودَانُ</foreign> is said in the R to denote [<hi rend="ital">The negroes;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that particular people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">race, who are the most stinking of mankind in the armpits and sweat,</hi> and the more so those who are eunuchs. (TA.) [It (i. e. <foreign lang="ar">السودان</foreign>) is also sometimes used for <foreign lang="ar">أَرْضُ السُّودَانِ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">بِلَادُ السُّودَانِ</foreign>, (<hi rend="ital">The land,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the country, of the negroes,</hi>) or the like: it is thus used in the TA voce <foreign lang="ar">سَمْغَرَةُ</foreign>.] And the epithet <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign> is also applied by the Arabs to a thing that is <foreign lang="ar">أَخْضَر</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">green</hi>]; because it appears to be thus at a distance. (Msb. [See <foreign lang="ar">أَخْضَرُ</foreign>: and see <foreign lang="ar">حَدِيقَةٌ دَهْمَآءُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُدْهَامَّةٌ</foreign>, voce <foreign lang="ar">أَدْهَمُ</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ القَلْبِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَوْدَآؤُهُ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">سَوَادٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [And <foreign lang="ar">السَّوْدَآءُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The black bile; one of the four humours of the body;</hi> of which the others are the yellow bile (<foreign lang="ar">الصَّفْرَآءُ</foreign>), the blood (<foreign lang="ar">الدَّمُ</foreign>), and the phlegm (<foreign lang="ar">البَلْغَمُ</foreign>).]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign> as opposed to <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَرُ</foreign> [and meaning The <hi rend="ital">Arab race,</hi> and also, accord. to some, in this case also, the <hi rend="ital">black</hi>]: see <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَرُ</foreign>, in two places.          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  As applied to a certain bird: see <foreign lang="ar">سُودَانِيَّةٌ</foreign>, in two places.          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  Also, as a subst., (S,) or an epithet in which the quality of a subst. predominates, (Sh, M,) so that it is used as a subst., (Sh, TA,) but imperfectly decl., (TA,) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">A great serpent,</hi> (S, M, K,) <hi rend="ital">in which is blackness:</hi> (S, M:) the <hi rend="ital">worst and greatest and most noxious of serpents, than which there is none more daring, for sometimes it opposes itself to a company of travellers, and follows the voice, and it is that which seeks retaliation, and he who is bitten by it will not escape death:</hi> (Sh, TA:) it is pluralized as a subst., (Sh, S, M,) its pl. being <foreign lang="ar">أَسَاوِدُ</foreign> (S, M) and <foreign lang="ar">أَسَاوِيدُ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21189-6" target="أَسْوَدَاتٌ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21191"/></foreign>: (M:) were it an epithet [used as such], its pl. would be <foreign lang="ar">سُودٌ</foreign>: it is also called <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ سَالِحٌ</foreign>, because it casts off its slough every year: you do not say <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَالِخٍ</foreign>: (S:) the female is called   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21189-7" target="أَسْوَدَةٌ" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21190"/></foreign>, (S, M,) which is extr.; (M;) and to this the epithet <foreign lang="ar">سَالِخَةٌ</foreign> is not applied. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الأَسْوَدَانِ</foreign> means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The serpent and the scorpion;</hi> (Sh, Mgh, Msb, K;) which are to be killed during prayer: (Sh, Mgh, Msb:) so called by the attribution of predominance [to the former]. (Sh, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  And <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Dates and water;</hi> (El-Ahmar, As, S, M, A, Mgh, Msb, K;) both together being thus called by a term which properly applies to one only, [accord. to some,] for [they say that] <foreign lang="ar">الأَسْوَدُ</foreign> alone signifies <hi rend="ital">dates,</hi> not water, and especially, or mostly, <hi rend="ital">the dates of El-Medeeneh;</hi> and in like manner, Aboo-Bekr and 'Omar together are called <foreign lang="ar">العُمَرَانِ</foreign>; and the sun and the moon together, <foreign lang="ar">القَمَرَانِ</foreign>: (TA:) or, as some say, it means <hi rend="ital">water and milk;</hi> and is applied by a rájiz to <hi rend="ital">water and the herb called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الفَثّ</foreign>, of [the grain of] which bread is made, and is eaten [in time of dearth or drought]. (M, L.) See also <foreign lang="ar">سُوَيْدٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  Also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَرَّة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">tract strewn with black and crumbling stones</hi>] <hi rend="ital">and night:</hi> (S, M, L:) so called because of their blackness. (M, L.) A party came as guests to Muzebbid El-Medenee, and he said to them, “ There is nothing for you with us but the <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدَانِ</foreign>: ” and they replied, “ Verily therein is a sufficiency: dates and water: ” but he said, “ I meant not that: I only meant the <foreign lang="ar">حَرَّة</foreign> and the night. ” (S, M.) And as to the saying of 'Áïsheh, that she was with the Prophet when they had no food, but only the <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدَانِ</foreign>, which is expl. by the lexicologists as meaning dates and water, [and thus by Mtr in the Mgh, ISd says,] in my opinion she only meant the <foreign lang="ar">حَرَّة</foreign> and night. (M.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ أَسْوَدُ الكَبِدِ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He is black-livered</hi>] means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">he is an enemy:</hi> (A, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">سُودُ الأَكْبَادِ</foreign> means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">enemies.</hi> (M, A.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  You say also, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ فُلَانٌ بِغَنَمِهِ سُودَ البُطُونِ</foreign>, and, in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرَ الكُلَى</foreign>, both meaning <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Such a one brought his sheep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goats, in a lean,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an emaciated, state.</hi> (As, S, and A in art. <foreign lang="ar">حمر</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">رَمَى بِسَهْمِهِ الأَسْوَدِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He shot with his lucky arrow,</hi> (A, K,) <hi rend="ital">that was smeared with blood,</hi> (A,) <hi rend="ital">by means of which he looked for good fortune,</hi> (K, TA,) because he had shot with it and hit the object shot at, (TA,) or as though it were black (K, TA) with blood, (TA,) or by its having been much handled. (K, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">كَلَّمْتُهُ فَمَا رَدَّ عَلَىَّ سَوْدَآءَ وَلَا بَيْضَآءَ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">I spoke to him, and he did not return to me a bad word nor a good one:</hi> (S, L:) or <hi rend="ital">a single word.</hi> (A.)          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَطْأَةٌ سَوْدَآءُ</foreign> means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A footstep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">footprint, that is becoming effaced:</hi> a recent one is termed <foreign lang="ar">حَمْرَآءُ</foreign>. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="15">-b15-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">السَّوْدَآءُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Cultivated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">planted, land;</hi> opposed to <foreign lang="ar">البَيْضَآءُ</foreign> [q. v.]. (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">بيض</foreign> [See also <foreign lang="ar">سَوْدَةٌ</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="16">-b16-</sense>  [But <foreign lang="ar">سَنَةٌ سَوْدَآءُ</foreign> means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A very severe year; more severe than such as is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَمْرَآءُ</foreign>; which is more severe than the <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضآء</foreign>, and still more so than the <foreign lang="ar">شَهْبَآء</foreign>: see arts. <foreign lang="ar">شهب</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">حمر</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="17">-b17-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الحَبَّةُ السَّوْدَآءُ</foreign>, said in a <pb n="1464"/> trad. to be a remedy for every disease except death, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشُّونِيزُ</foreign> [q. v.], (K,) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21189-8" target="السُّوَيْدَآءُ" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (TA,) [i. e.] this latter signifies <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّةُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشُّونِيزِ</foreign>, (M,) or properly <foreign lang="ar">الشِّينِيز</foreign>, for thus the Arabs called it accord. to IAar: or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحَبَّةُ الخَضْرَآءُ</foreign> [q. v. in art. <foreign lang="ar">حب</foreign>], because the Arabs [often] call black <foreign lang="ar">أَخْضَر</foreign>, and green <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَد</foreign>. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  It is also used as an epithet denoting excess; but as such is anomalous, being formed from a verb whence the simple epithet is of the measure <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعَلُ</foreign>: so in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ مِنْ حَلَكِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الغُرَابِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Blacker than the blackness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">intense blackness, of the crow,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">raven:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">حَلَكٌ</foreign>]. (I'Ak p. 237.
